## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, matching second-order ODE models of (non)linear oscillators. Typical structures combine restoring forces in x, damping terms in v, and optional external driving/parametric excitation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; sign absorbed in c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper dynamics)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening nonlinearity plus damping)
- General polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (multi-well or strong nonlinearity approximations)
- Pendulum equation (exact): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (rotational oscillator where restoring torque is sinusoidal in angle)
- Quadratic/drag-like damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic damping magnitude grows with speed)
- Coulomb (dry-friction) damping surrogate: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (smoothed sign(v) friction term)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excitation controlled by velocity-dependent damping)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodically forced resonance)
- Biharmonic/quasiperiodic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (multi-tone forcing responses)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd restoring force symmetry (x -> -x gives dv_dt -> -dv_dt when v=0) suggests terms like x, x**3, x**5 and/or sin(c*x).
- Hardening vs softening stiffness can often be distinguished by the sign of the x**3 coefficient (frequency increases or decreases with amplitude).
- Velocity-proportional damping produces exponential decay of oscillation amplitude and is captured by a linear v term in dv_dt.
- Speed-dependent dissipation (e.g., aerodynamic drag) is indicated by v*Abs(v) or higher odd powers of v in dv_dt.
- Self-excited limit cycles typically arise from state-dependent damping such as (c - x**2)*v (van der Pol) or (c - v**2)*v (Rayleigh).
- External periodic forcing leaves a clear time-only signature in dv_dt, commonly sinusoidal terms in t (cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) that persist even when x≈0 and v≈0.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when stiffness-like terms multiply x with a periodic function of t, i.e., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x.
- Dry friction or stick-slip effects often manifest as nearly constant-magnitude opposing acceleration for small v, modeled by tanh(c*v) (smooth) or sign-like behavior.
